# Codex iter 1 — I-gen-005 Step 1.5 diff review (telemetry fix)

## §8.3.1 canonical cap directive (verbatim)

```
HARD ITERATION CAP: 5 per document. This is iter 1 of 5.
- Front-load ALL real findings in iter 1. No drip-feeding across iterations.
- Same quality bar regardless of iteration count.
- "Don't pick bone from egg" — reserve P0/P1 for real execution risks.
- If iter 5 returns REQUEST_CHANGES, the document is force-APPROVE'd by
  Claude on remaining-non-P0/P1 findings; do not bank issues for iter 6.
- Verdict APPROVE iff zero NOVEL P0 AND zero continuing P0 AND zero P1.
```

## What you flagged in the smoke review (2026-05-26)

> P1: `verification_details.json` is not the final per-sentence
> provenance artifact. It is reconstructed by re-running bare
> strict_verify on `sr.rewritten_draft`
> (`scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py:2703-2721`) after the pipeline has
> already applied repair/dedup/regen paths. The emitted report
> contains sentences logged as dropped (`report.md:9` vs
> `verification_details.json:173` and `verification_details.json:200`),
> and the section-list counts do not match artifact totals.
>
> proposed_fix: Persist final `SectionResult.kept_sentences_pre_resolve`
> plus final dropped accounting from the generation pipeline, or add
> final dropped sentence objects to `SectionResult`; do not reconstruct
> final verification details by re-running bare strict_verify on
> rewritten drafts.

## What I changed (your proposed fix, implemented)

### 1. `src/polaris_graph/generator/multi_section_generator.py:79-118` — SectionResult fields

Added two FINAL-state tracking fields to SectionResult:

```python
# Per-section FINAL dropped sentences with full SV objects (.sentence,
# .tokens, .failure_reasons). Reflects post-dedup pipeline state.
dropped_sentences_final: list[Any] = field(default_factory=list)
# Sentences dropped by fact_dedup as redundant (LLM consolidation,
# NOT strict_verify failures — tracked separately so the operator
# can see WHY each missing sentence is missing).
dropped_sentences_dedup_redundant: list[str] = field(default_factory=list)
```

### 2. `multi_section_generator.py:1456-1462` — populate at initial strict_verify

```python
return SectionResult(
    ...
    kept_sentences_pre_resolve=list(report.kept_sentences),
    dropped_sentences_final=list(report.dropped_sentences),   # NEW
)
```

### 3. `multi_section_generator.py:~3845` — extend at dedup re-verify

When `_fact_dedup_pass`'s LLM rewrites fail re-strict_verify, those
SVs are now appended to `sr.dropped_sentences_final` (real
strict_verify failures, not consolidations):

```python
sr.dropped_sentences_final.extend(rewrite_report.dropped_sentences)
```

### 4. `multi_section_generator.py:~3865` — track dedup-redundants separately

When `_fact_dedup_pass` removes a redundant via LLM consolidation
(NOT a strict_verify failure), capture the string in the dedup-only
field:

```python
final_str_set = {sv.sentence for sv in final_svs}
sr.dropped_sentences_dedup_redundant.extend(
    s for s in original_strs if s not in final_str_set
)
```

### 5. `scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py:2703-2762` — serialize FROM SectionResult

Replaced the bare `strict_verify(sr.rewritten_draft, ev_pool)` re-run
with direct serialization of the FINAL `SectionResult` fields. Added
a separate `dropped_by_dedup_redundant[]` section in the JSON output
plus a `dedup_redundant_count` rollup so the operator can distinguish
the two drop categories.

## Unit test — 8 assertions, all PASS

`scripts/test_i_gen_005_step15_telemetry.py`:

```
PASS: verified sentence is in kept[]
PASS: real strict_verify failure is in dropped[] with failure_reasons
PASS: dedup-redundant is NOT in dropped[] (the pre-fix bug)
PASS: dedup-redundant IS tracked in dropped_by_dedup_redundant[]
PASS: total_kept = 1, total_dropped = 2 (real_failure + dedup_redundant)
PASS: drop_reason_counts excludes dedup-redundant
PASS: dedup_redundant_count = 1
PASS: kept and dedup-redundant cover the same fact (15 mg / 2.30%)
```

The fixture mimics the EXACT bug you flagged: 3 sentences in the
rewritten_draft, 1 kept after dedup, 1 consolidated into the kept one
(dedup-redundant), 1 real strict_verify failure (cancer-50%
fabrication). The pre-fix code would have FALSELY listed the
dedup-redundant in `dropped[]` with bogus failure_reasons (because
re-running strict_verify on the rewritten_draft would have judged it
on its own). The post-fix code correctly routes it to
`dropped_by_dedup_redundant[]`.

   dedup-vs-strict-verify distinction is now captured. Does the
   schema (separate `dropped[]` and `dropped_by_dedup_redundant[]`)
   match what you wanted?

   regen replaces a section result entirely (`section_results[idx] =
   regen_result`), the prior result's dropped sentences are lost. Is
   that acceptable for now, or should regen also preserve historical
   drops?

3. **Should `total_in` be the rewritten_draft sentence count** (the
   original strict_verify input), or the post-dedup count? Currently
   I use `kept + strict_dropped + dedup_redundant` which approximates
   the rewritten_draft sentence count. Is that the right semantic?

4. **Any NEW findings** in the iter-1 diff? P0/P1 only — don't pick
   bone from egg.

5. **Approval to commit Step 1 + Step 1.5 together** on a fresh
   branch, then re-run smoke to verify the telemetry now matches the
   emitted report?

877:             _allow_lists = build_allow_lists(evidence_subset)
878:             if _allow_lists:
879:                 system = system + "\n\n" + format_allow_list_for_prompt(_allow_lists)
880:         except Exception as _allow_exc:
881:             # Fail-soft: if extraction errors, fall through to the
882:             # generator without the constraint block (caller already
883:             # has HARD CONTRACT + cold-temp lever). Log loudly.
884:             logger.warning(
885:                 "[multi_section] I-gen-005 allow-list build failed for "
886:                 "section %r: %s — proceeding without allow-list",
887:                 section.title, _allow_exc,
888:             )

890:     # V32 M-71: inject section-local contradiction-hedging hints.
891:     if contradictions:
892:         from .contradiction_hedging import (
893:             filter_section_contradictions,
894:             render_section_hedging_block,
895:         )

897:             section.title, contradictions,

899:         hedging_block = render_section_hedging_block(hints)

904:                 len(hints), section.title,

925:     # I-gen-005 (#904): re-add the HARD OUTPUT CONTRACT for reasoning-first

372: def parse_provenance_tokens(sentence: str) -> list[ProvenanceToken]:
373:     """Extract all [#ev:id:start-end] tokens from a sentence."""
374:     return [
375:         ProvenanceToken(
1238: 
1239:     Handles trailing citation markers like `.[1]`, `.[#ev:ev_a:0-5]`,
1240:     `.[1][2]` — the second alternative in the split regex triggers on
1241:     the closing `]` so the marker stays attached to the preceding
1242:     sentence rather than being eaten.
1243:     """
1244:     if not text:
1245:         return []
1246:     parts = _SENTENCE_SPLIT_RE.split(text.strip())
1247:     return [p.strip() for p in parts if p.strip()]

1259: def split_findings_and_limitations(text: str) -> tuple[str, str]:
1260:     """Split a draft into (findings_text, limitations_text).
1261: 
1262:     Gap-3: the generator now writes a "Limitations:" paragraph that
1263:     discusses pipeline telemetry (tier mix, contradictions) without
1264:     per-sentence [ev_XXX] markers. Verification should be relaxed for
1265:     that paragraph — no citation tokens are required.
1266: 
1267:     Returns ("findings text", "limitations text"). If no Limitations
1268:     block is found, returns (full_text, "").
1269:     """
1270:     if not text:
1271:         return "", ""
1272:     # Find the literal word "Limitations:" at start of a line or after
1273:     # whitespace. Case-insensitive, allow markdown heading variants.
1274:     m = re.search(
1275:         r"(^|\n\s*)(?:#{0,3}\s*)?(?:\*\*)?Limitations(?:\*\*)?\s*:",
1276:         text, re.IGNORECASE,
1277:     )
1278:     if not m:
1279:         return text.strip(), ""
1280:     findings = text[:m.start()].strip()
1281:     limitations = text[m.start():].strip()
1282:     return findings, limitations
1283: 
1284: 
1285: def verify_limitations_sentence_against_telemetry(
1286:     sentence: str,
1287:     telemetry_block: str,
1288: ) -> SentenceVerification:
1289:     """BUG-M-204 fix (deep-dive R10): check that every decimal / integer
1290:     quoted in a Limitations sentence appears verbatim in the telemetry
1291:     block. Sentences that make unsupported numeric claims about the
1292:     pipeline's own corpus are dropped, not passed through.
1293: 
1294:     Returns SentenceVerification with is_verified=True/False.
1295:     """
1296:     import re as _re
1297:     tokens = parse_provenance_tokens(sentence)
1298:     # Extract all decimal-or-integer numeric literals from the sentence.
1299:     # Allow percentages; strip '%'.
1300:     sentence_nums = _re.findall(
1301:         r"(?<![A-Za-z\d])-?\d+(?:\.\d+)?(?:%)?", sentence,
1302:     )
1303:     # Only include numbers that are NOT trivial (e.g., "1" in "table 1"
1304:     # isn't a claim; 3+ digit or decimal is more likely a real number).
1305:     substantive = [n for n in sentence_nums if
1306:                    len(n.replace("-", "").replace("%", "").replace(".", "")) >= 2
1307:                    or "." in n or "%" in n]
1308: 
1309:     failures: list[str] = []
1310:     if not telemetry_block:
1311:         # No telemetry to check against; treat as pass-through (backward
1312:         # compat when caller doesn't pass the block).
1313:         return SentenceVerification(
1314:             sentence=sentence, tokens=tokens,
1315:             is_verified=True, failure_reasons=[],
1316:             soft_warnings=["limitations_pass_through_no_telemetry"],
1317:         )
1318:     # BUG-M-209 fix (pass 2 remediation): the telemetry block is a
1319:     # whitelist of known metric KEYS. A numeric literal in a Limitations
1320:     # sentence must appear close to a known metric keyword, not just
1321:     # anywhere in telemetry. "T-cell count 500" should NOT pass when
1322:     # telemetry says "http_status: 500".
1323:     #
1324:     # Known telemetry metric anchors, case-insensitive:
1325:     _TELEMETRY_METRIC_KEYS = (
1326:         "tier_distribution",
1327:         "t1", "t2", "t3", "t4", "t5", "t6", "t7",
1328:         "unknown",  # UNKNOWN tier
1329:         "contradictions_detected", "contradictions",
1330:         "rel_diff", "relative_difference",
1331:         "severity",
1332:         "date_range",
1333:         "completeness_gaps", "uncovered", "uncovered_topic",
1334:     )
1335:     telemetry_lower = telemetry_block.lower()
1336:     telemetry_lines = telemetry_lower.split("\n")
1337: 
1338:     def _line_mentions_metric(line: str) -> bool:
1339:         for key in _TELEMETRY_METRIC_KEYS:
1340:             if key in line:
1341:                 return True
1342:         return False
1343: 
1344:     for num in substantive:
1345:         bare = num.rstrip("%")
1346:         bare_escaped = _re.escape(bare)
1347:         num_escaped = _re.escape(num)
1348:         # Check every line that contains the number. The number counts
1349:         # as "backed by telemetry" only if THAT line mentions a known
1350:         # telemetry metric key.
1351:         matched = False
1352:         for line in telemetry_lines:
1353:             has_bare = _re.search(
1354:                 rf"(?<![\d.]){bare_escaped}(?![\d])", line,
1355:             )
1356:             has_pct = (num != bare) and _re.search(
1357:                 rf"(?<![\d.]){num_escaped}(?![\d])", line,
1358:             )
1359:             if (has_bare or has_pct) and _line_mentions_metric(line):
1360:                 matched = True
1361:                 break
1362:         if not matched:
1363:             failures.append(f"limitations_number_not_in_telemetry:{num}")
1364: 
1365:     if failures:
1366:         return SentenceVerification(
1367:             sentence=sentence, tokens=tokens,
1368:             is_verified=False, failure_reasons=failures,
1369:             soft_warnings=["limitations_paragraph"],
1370:         )
1371:     return SentenceVerification(
1372:         sentence=sentence, tokens=tokens,
1373:         is_verified=True, failure_reasons=[],
1374:         soft_warnings=["limitations_paragraph_verified"],
1375:     )
1376:

1378: def strict_verify(
1379:     draft_text: str,
1380:     evidence_pool: dict[str, dict[str, Any]],
1381:     *,
1382:     require_number_match: bool = True,
1383:     telemetry_block: str | None = None,
1384: ) -> StrictVerificationReport:
1385:     """Run strict verification on a draft. Drops failing sentences.
1386: 
1387:     Gap-3 (original): the Limitations paragraph was pass-through because
1388:     it discusses pipeline telemetry, not evidence.
1389: 
1390:     BUG-M-204 fix (deep-dive R10): when `telemetry_block` is supplied,
1391:     Limitations sentences ARE verified against it — every numeric
1392:     claim in the sentence must appear verbatim in the telemetry block.
1393:     This catches a fabricated "only 3% of sources are T1" claim when
1394:     the telemetry actually says "T1: 9%". Backward-compatible: if
1395:     telemetry_block is None (default), falls back to pass-through.
1396:     """
1397:     findings_text, limitations_text = split_findings_and_limitations(draft_text)
1398: 
1399:     kept: list[SentenceVerification] = []
1400:     dropped: list[SentenceVerification] = []
1401: 
1402:     # Findings: strict provenance verification
1403:     findings_sentences = split_into_sentences(findings_text)
1404:     for s in findings_sentences:
1405:         v = verify_sentence_provenance(
1406:             s, evidence_pool,
1407:             require_number_match=require_number_match,
1408:         )
1409:         if v.is_verified:
1410:             kept.append(v)
1411:         else:
1412:             dropped.append(v)
1413: 
1414:     # Limitations: telemetry-grounded verification if block supplied,
1415:     # else pass-through (M-204 backward-compat).
1416:     limitations_sentences = split_into_sentences(limitations_text)
1417:     for s in limitations_sentences:
1418:         if telemetry_block is not None:
1419:             v = verify_limitations_sentence_against_telemetry(
1420:                 s, telemetry_block,
1421:             )
1422:             if v.is_verified:
1423:                 kept.append(v)
1424:             else:
1425:                 dropped.append(v)
1426:         else:
1427:             tokens = parse_provenance_tokens(s)
1428:             kept.append(SentenceVerification(
1429:                 sentence=s,
1430:                 tokens=tokens,
1431:                 is_verified=True,
1432:                 failure_reasons=[],
1433:                 soft_warnings=["limitations_paragraph_pass_through"],
1434:             ))
1435: 
1436:     total_in = len(findings_sentences) + len(limitations_sentences)
1437:     return StrictVerificationReport(
1438:         kept_sentences=kept,
1439:         dropped_sentences=dropped,
1440:         total_in=total_in,
1441:         total_kept=len(kept),
1442:         total_dropped=len(dropped),
1443:     )

623:                     ev.get("statement"),
624:                     ev.get("title"),
625:                     label,
626:                     primary_ev,
627:                 ]
628:                 statement = next(
629:                     (s for s in statement_candidates if s), primary_ev,
630:                 )

638:                 })

src\polaris_graph\generator\multi_section_generator.py:250:- **M-40: Mechanism section is the narrative-depth lever.** When AT LEAST 3 evidence rows in the summary above contain mechanism-of-action vocabulary — in either the `title:` field or the statement body — you MUST include "Mechanism" as one of the outline sections (5 by default, 6 when regulatory evidence is also present per M-41a above). Trigger vocabulary (any of, case-insensitive): "mechanism", "pharmacokinetic", "pharmacodynamic", "receptor", "half-life", "bioavailability", "metabolism", "agonist", "antagonist", "binding", "signaling", "pathway", "kinetic". A research-grade synthesis explains WHY the intervention works, not only WHETHER it works. Top-tier Deep Research outputs (GPT-5.4 DR, Gemini 3.1 Pro DR) dedicate a full section to mechanism/pharmacology for any clinical efficacy question; a report without it reads as a short brief rather than a deep synthesis. This rule is generalizable: in materials/chemistry a Mechanism section covers reaction pathway / phase transition / interface chemistry; in policy it covers causal pathway / incentive mechanism / enforcement mechanism; in finance it covers transmission channel / market microstructure.

2364: def _merge_bibliographies(
2365:     section_slices: list[list[dict[str, Any]]],
2366: ) -> list[dict[str, Any]]:
2367:     """Merge per-section biblios into a single ordered bibliography,
2368:     remapping section-local citation numbers to global numbers."""
2369:     # Each section's biblio has its own 1-based numbering. We need to
2370:     # renumber globally, but the section's verified_text already has
2371:     # [1][2][3] markers in section-local space.
2372:     # Simpler approach: return the raw per-section biblios flattened,
2373:     # deduped by evidence_id, and let the caller remap the inline
2374:     # markers in a separate pass.
2375:     seen: dict[str, dict[str, Any]] = {}
2376:     for sl in section_slices:
2377:         for entry in sl:
2378:             ev_id = entry.get("evidence_id", "")
2379:             if ev_id and ev_id not in seen:
2380:                 seen[ev_id] = dict(entry)
2381:     # Renumber globally
2382:     final: list[dict[str, Any]] = []
2383:     for i, entry in enumerate(seen.values(), 1):
2384:         new_entry = dict(entry)
2385:         new_entry["num"] = i
2386:         final.append(new_entry)
2387:     return final
2388:

2390: def _remap_section_markers_to_global(
2391:     section_results: list[SectionResult],
2392:     global_biblio: list[dict[str, Any]],
2393: ) -> list[str]:
2394:     """Rewrite each section's [N] markers from section-local to global.
2395: 
2396:     Returns a list of remapped section prose strings.
2397:     """
2398:     ev_to_global = {b["evidence_id"]: b["num"] for b in global_biblio}
2399:     remapped: list[str] = []
2400:     for sect in section_results:
2401:         if not sect.verified_text:
2402:             continue
2403:         # Build a mapping section-local-num -> global-num
2404:         local_to_global: dict[int, int] = {}
2405:         for entry in sect.biblio_slice:
2406:             local_num = entry.get("num")
2407:             ev_id = entry.get("evidence_id", "")
2408:             global_num = ev_to_global.get(ev_id)
2409:             if local_num is not None and global_num is not None:
2410:                 local_to_global[local_num] = global_num
2411:         text = sect.verified_text
2412: 
2413:         # Replace [N] markers using the mapping. Do the replace with a
2414:         # callable to avoid subsequent substitutions clobbering each
2415:         # other (e.g., [1] -> [5] -> [15]).
2416:         def _replace(match: re.Match) -> str:
2417:             n = int(match.group(1))
2418:             g = local_to_global.get(n)
2419:             return f"[{g}]" if g else match.group(0)
2420: 
2421:         text = re.sub(r"\[(\d+)\]", _replace, text)
2422:         remapped.append(text)
2423:     return remapped

src\polaris_graph\generator\multi_section_generator.py:693:12b. **Claim-frame hard constraint (M-38, eliminating under-framed study mentions)**: Rule #12 is asymmetric and STRICT — when you name a specific study, trial, cohort, or experiment by its short name (phase-N trial identifier in clinical; long-run battery cycling test in materials; named longitudinal cohort in epidemiology; named regulatory docket in policy), that sentence — or the IMMEDIATELY PRECEDING sentence in the same paragraph — MUST carry at LEAST THREE frame elements drawn from: sample size / cohort N; baseline value; comparator / control arm; specific dose or intervention level; primary endpoint; timepoint; effect size WITH uncertainty (CI, SD, or p-value). If you cannot produce three of those elements from the cited evidence, DO NOT name the study by its short name — phrase the sentence generically as "one randomized trial showed ... [ev_X]" or "a prospective cohort in the target population reported ... [ev_X]" or "one pooled analysis found ... [ev_X]" or "a long-run cycling test reported ... [ev_X]" instead. This hard floor prevents the failure mode where a sentence names a specific study but gives only a single effect-size number without N, baseline, or comparator — producing a news-style summary mis-labelled with a primary-study name. Concrete templates (use placeholders): GOOD: "In [STUDY NAME] (N=[SAMPLE_SIZE], baseline [PRIMARY_METRIC]=[BASELINE_VALUE]), [INTERVENTION_ARM] reduced [ENDPOINT] by [EFFECT_SIZE] versus [COMPARATOR_ARM] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." GOOD (generic when frame is unavailable): "A pre-planned pooled analysis of two phase-3 trials reported [ENDPOINT]=[VALUE] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — no short-name attribution because pooled data lack per-trial N. BAD (under-framed, must be rewritten): "[STUDY NAME] showed that [INTERVENTION] reduced [ENDPOINT] more than [COMPARATOR] [ev_X]." — names the study with only one frame element (effect direction); rewrite as "A head-to-head trial of [INTERVENTION] versus [COMPARATOR] reported greater [ENDPOINT] reduction with [INTERVENTION] [ev_X]" which drops the study name because the frame is too thin. BAD (under-framed, must be rewritten): "[STUDY NAME] found median time to [THRESHOLD] was [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — names study with only endpoint + effect; rewrite as "One pooled analysis of two phase-3 trials found median time to [THRESHOLD] was [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]" ONLY if the cited evidence confirms pooled data across two trials. This rule is what converts a LOSE_BOTH on Claim frames into a competitive synthesis.
src\polaris_graph\generator\multi_section_generator.py:694:12c. **Anaphoric and group claim-frame enforcement (M-42a, extending rule #12b to bypass patterns)**: Rule #12b fires only on explicit short-name study tokens (e.g. specific phase-3 trial identifiers like [STUDY NAME]-N). Sentences using ANAPHORIC references ("This trial", "The same trial", "The study also reported", "That analysis") or GROUP references ("the [PROGRAM] trials", "the phase-3 program", "pivotal trials") bypass that rule and reintroduce the under-framed pattern. This extension closes the bypass:  (A) An ANAPHORIC sentence referring to a specific study must EITHER (a) include at least ONE frame element (sample size, baseline, comparator, dose, endpoint, timepoint, or effect-size-with-uncertainty) in the SAME sentence, OR (b) be placed IMMEDIATELY AFTER a sentence that names the specific study with >=3 frame elements (the antecedent provides framing context). A bare anaphoric sentence with no antecedent framing context is FORBIDDEN. (B) A GROUP reference like "the [PROGRAM] trials" or "the phase-3 program" does NOT inherit from a single prior study's framing. The sentence must EITHER (a) ENUMERATE the specific studies inline — e.g. "the [PROGRAM] trials ([STUDY]-1, -2, -3) pooled N=[SAMPLE_SIZE]" — OR (b) present a pooled / program-level claim with POOLED N AND POOLED effect size stated inline (e.g. "across the [N_TRIALS] pivotal trials pooled N=[SAMPLE_SIZE] adults with [CONDITION], [ENDPOINT] reduction was [EFFECT_SIZE]"). Both parts of the rule apply across domains: in materials/chemistry "these composites" or "the second-gen samples" inherit similarly; in policy "the CMS rules" or "the parallel rulemakings" do. Concrete examples (placeholders only): GOOD: "In [STUDY NAME] (N=[SAMPLE_SIZE], baseline [METRIC]=[BASELINE_VALUE]), [INTERVENTION_ARM] reduced [ENDPOINT] by [EFFECT_SIZE] versus [COMPARATOR_ARM] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]. The same trial also reported [SECONDARY_ENDPOINT]=[VALUE] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — second sentence is anaphoric but inherits frame from first. GOOD: "Across the [STUDY]-1, -2, -3, and -4 pooled population (N=[SAMPLE_SIZE]), median time to [THRESHOLD] was [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — group reference with pooled N inline. BAD: "This trial also reported maintained [ENDPOINT] [ev_X]." — anaphoric sentence with no antecedent frame. BAD: "The [PROGRAM] trials found greater [ENDPOINT] reduction with [INTERVENTION] [ev_X]." — group reference without enumeration or pooled N.

1043: 
1044: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
1045: # M-41c: deterministic claim-frame post-check
1046: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
1047: 
1048: 
1049: # Trial short-name pattern. Generalizable across clinical trial programs —
1050: # any ALL-CAPS token followed by a hyphen-digit suffix counts, plus a
1051: # small list of famous all-letters names. No drug-specific tokens.
1052: #
1053: # M-41c pass-2 (Codex audit medium #1): exclude standards-body /
1054: # engineering-identifier tokens that would false-positive match the
1055: # hyphen-digit pattern (ISO-9001, IEC-62109, DIN-17100, ASTM-D412,
1056: # ANSI-C, IEEE-754, NCT- prefixes, SAE-J series). These are technical
1057: # identifiers, not named clinical trials, and dropping sentences that
1058: # cite them would remove legitimate standards-mentioning prose.
1059: _M41C_TRIAL_NAME_DENYLIST: frozenset[str] = frozenset({
1060:     "ISO", "IEC", "DIN", "ASTM", "ANSI", "IEEE", "SAE", "EN", "BS",
1061:     "UL", "JIS", "GB", "CAS", "ICH", "OECD", "USP", "EP", "USC",
1062:     "CFR", "EU", "US", "UN", "WHO", "FDA", "EMA", "NCT",
1063: })
1064: 
1065: _M41C_TRIAL_SHORT_NAME_RE = re.compile(
1066:     r"\b(?:"
1067:     r"[A-Z][A-Z0-9]{2,}-\d+(?:[A-Z]+)?"        # SURPASS-2, SURMOUNT-4, STEP-3
1068:     r"|[A-Z][A-Z0-9]{2,}-CVOT"                  # SURPASS-CVOT
1069:     r"|SELECT|LEADER|SUSTAIN|PIONEER|REWIND"    # famous all-letter names
1070:     r"|AWARD|GRADE|DEVOTE|HARMONY|CANVAS"
1071:     r"|DECLARE|EMPEROR"
1072:     r")\b",
1073: )
1074: 
1075: 
1076: # Frame-element detectors. A sentence is "framed" when it (or its
1077: # immediately preceding sentence) matches >=3 distinct classes.
1078: # Keep each class regex domain-agnostic; clinical-specific keywords
1079: # go in a permissive union with other-domain equivalents so the rule
1080: # generalizes beyond T2D trials.
1081: _M41C_FRAME_ELEMENT_PATTERNS: list[tuple[str, re.Pattern]] = [
1082:     (
1083:         "sample_size",
1084:         re.compile(
1085:             r"\bN\s*=\s*\d+\b"
1086:             r"|\b\d{2,}\s+(?:patients|participants|adults|subjects|"
1087:             r"enrolled|randomi[sz]ed|cases|samples|specimens)\b",
1088:             re.IGNORECASE,
1089:         ),
1090:     ),
1091:     (
1092:         "baseline",
1093:         re.compile(r"\bbaseline\b|\binitial\s+value\b", re.IGNORECASE),
1094:     ),
1095:     (
1096:         "comparator",
1097:         re.compile(
1098:             r"\b(?:vs|versus|compared\s+to|compared\s+with|"
1099:             r"against\s+placebo|non[-\s]inferior|superior\s+to|"
1100:             r"head[-\s]to[-\s]head|control\s+arm)\b",
1101:             re.IGNORECASE,
1102:         ),
1103:     ),
1104:     (
1105:         "dose_or_level",
1106:         re.compile(
1107:             r"\b\d+\.?\d*\s*(?:mg|mcg|µg|units|IU|kg|mmol|mol|nm|"
1108:             r"percent|wt%|ppm|mAh|MPa|GPa)\b",
1109:             re.IGNORECASE,
1110:         ),
1111:     ),
1112:     (
1113:         "endpoint",
1114:         re.compile(
1115:             r"\b(?:endpoint|primary\s+outcome|primary\s+efficacy|"
1116:             r"co-primary|key\s+secondary|HbA1c|body\s+weight|"
1117:             r"weight\s+loss|cardiovascular\s+outcome|MACE|cycle\s+life|"
1118:             r"capacity\s+retention|phase\s+transition|reaction\s+yield)\b",
1119:             re.IGNORECASE,
1120:         ),
1121:     ),
1122:     (
1123:         "timepoint",
1124:         re.compile(
1125:             r"\b(?:week|month|year|day)s?\s*\d+"
1126:             r"|\b\d+\s+(?:week|month|year|day)s?\b"
1127:             r"|\bat\s+(?:week|month|year)\s*\d+\b"
1128:             r"|\bover\s+\d+\s+(?:week|month|year)s?\b",
1129:             re.IGNORECASE,
1130:         ),
1131:     ),
1132:     (
1133:         "uncertainty",
1134:         re.compile(
1135:             r"p\s*[<>=]\s*0?\.\d+"                         # p<0.001
1136:             r"|\b\d+\s*%\s+CI\b"                           # 95% CI
1137:             r"|\bCI\s*[\(:]\s*"                            # CI (0.5 to 0.8)
1138:             r"|\b\(\s*\d+\.?\d*\s*(?:to|[-–])\s*\d+"       # (1.2 to 2.3)
1139:             r"|\bSD\s*\d|\bSE\s*\d"                        # SD 1.2
1140:             r"|±\s*\d",                                    # ±1.5
1141:             re.IGNORECASE,
1142:         ),
1143:     ),
1144: ]
1145: 
1146: 
1147: def _m41c_sentence_names_trial(sentence: str) -> bool:
1148:     """True when the sentence contains a specific-trial short-name
1149:     token (SURPASS-2, SURMOUNT-4, SELECT, etc.).
1150: 
1151:     M-41c pass-2: excludes standards-body identifier prefixes
1152:     (ISO-9001, IEC-62109, etc.) — these technical-standard tokens
1153:     pattern-match the hyphen-digit shape but are not named trials.
1154:     A match is trial-qualified only if the prefix before the `-` is
1155:     NOT in the denylist."""
1156:     for m in _M41C_TRIAL_SHORT_NAME_RE.finditer(sentence):
1157:         token = m.group(0)
1158:         # Split off prefix before the hyphen, if any. All-letter
1159:         # famous names (SELECT, LEADER, etc.) have no hyphen and are
1160:         # trial-qualified directly.
1161:         if "-" in token:
1162:             prefix = token.split("-", 1)[0]
1163:             if prefix in _M41C_TRIAL_NAME_DENYLIST:
1164:                 continue
1165:         return True
1166:     return False
1167: 
1168: 
1169: def _m41c_frame_element_count(sentence: str, prev_sentence: str = "") -> int:
1170:     """Return the number of DISTINCT frame-element classes present in
1171:     `sentence` + `prev_sentence` combined. Max return value equals
1172:     the number of classes in _M41C_FRAME_ELEMENT_PATTERNS (currently
1173:     7). A sentence with N=1879, baseline HbA1c 8.28%, vs semaglutide,
1174:     15 mg, HbA1c change, at week 40, p<0.001 would score 7."""
1175:     combined = f"{prev_sentence or ''} {sentence or ''}"
1176:     return sum(1 for _, pat in _M41C_FRAME_ELEMENT_PATTERNS if pat.search(combined))
1177: 
1178: 
1179: def filter_underframed_trial_sentences(
1180:     sentences: list[Any],
1181:     min_frame_elements: int = 3,
1182: ) -> tuple[list[Any], list[Any]]:
1183:     """M-41c: drop sentences that name a specific trial by short name
1184:     but carry fewer than `min_frame_elements` frame classes in the
1185:     sentence plus the immediately preceding sentence.
1186: 
1187:     Args:
1188:         sentences: list of objects with a `.sentence` string attribute
1189:             (typically SentenceVerification). Items without this
1190:             attribute are passed through untouched.
1191:         min_frame_elements: required distinct frame-element classes.
1192:             Default 3 matches the M-38 prompt-rule floor.
1193: 
1194:     Returns:
1195:         (kept, dropped) — kept preserves input order; dropped is the
1196:         list of under-framed trial sentences removed.
1197: 
1198:     Non-trial sentences are always kept. A sentence naming a trial
1199:     that has enough frame elements (>=3 classes) is kept. A sentence
1200:     naming a trial without enough framing is dropped. This is the
1201:     code-level enforcement of the M-38 prompt rule: the prompt asks
1202:     the LLM to drop the short-name attribution; if the LLM doesn't,
1203:     M-41c removes the sentence post-verify.
1204:     """
1205:     kept: list[Any] = []
1206:     dropped: list[Any] = []
1207:     for i, sv in enumerate(sentences):
1208:         text = getattr(sv, "sentence", None)
1209:         if not isinstance(text, str) or not text.strip():
1210:             kept.append(sv)
1211:             continue
1212:         if not _m41c_sentence_names_trial(text):
1213:             kept.append(sv)
1214:             continue
1215:         prev_text = ""
1216:         if i > 0:
1217:             prev_text = getattr(sentences[i - 1], "sentence", "") or ""
1218:         if _m41c_frame_element_count(text, prev_text) >= min_frame_elements:
1219:             kept.append(sv)
1220:         else:
1221:             dropped.append(sv)
1222:     return kept, dropped
1223: 
1224:

 succeeded in 803ms:
1: """Cross-section fact-dedup pass — GH#423 I-gen-002.
2: 
3: After all multi_section generation completes (parallel asyncio.gather)
4: but BEFORE strict_verify drops bad sentences, this module:
5: 
6:   1. Extracts a numeric-token signature per sentence (percentages,
7:      dollar amounts bucketed by ±5%, years).
8:   2. Groups sentences across sections by signature.
9:   3. For each group with len > 1: marks the FIRST section's instance
10:      as PRIMARY, all others as REDUNDANT.
11:   4. Issues a SINGLE batched LLM call to rewrite REDUNDANT sentences
12:      as cross-references (e.g., "as noted under Efficacy [ev_X]").
13:   5. Returns updated sections with redundant sentences replaced.
14: 
15: Failure handling: if the rewrite LLM call fails or returns malformed
16: output, fall back to keeping the PRIMARY only and DROPPING all
17: REDUNDANTS. This is the safe degradation per Codex review
18: (GH#423 quality analysis, .codex/I-gen-002/codex_path_quality_output.txt
19: strict_verify_interaction=8/10, failure_modes=8/10).
20: 
21: Section ordering for PRIMARY selection: the order returned by the
22: caller (typically the outline-defined order: Efficacy → Comparative
23: → Regulatory → Population Subgroups → Long-term Outcomes for policy
24: templates; Efficacy → Safety → Comparative → Mechanism → Regulatory
25: for clinical). The first-section-in-order wins for any duplicate
26: fact.
27: """
28: from __future__ import annotations
29: 
30: import logging
31: import re
32: from dataclasses import dataclass, field
33: from typing import Any, Callable, Optional
34: 
35: logger = logging.getLogger("polaris_graph.fact_dedup")
36: 
37: 
38: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
39: # Numeric-token extraction
40: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
41: 
42: # Percentages: "8.7%", "8.7 percent", "8.7 per cent"
43: _PERCENT_RE = re.compile(
44:     r"(\d+(?:\.\d+)?)\s*(?:%|per[ \-]?cent\b|percent\b)",
45:     re.IGNORECASE,
46: )
47: 
48: # Dollar amounts: "$200", "$1.4 billion", "CAD $700 million", "USD 299M"
49: _DOLLAR_RE = re.compile(
50:     r"(?:\$|\bUSD\s*|\bCAD\s*)\s*"
51:     r"(\d+(?:[.,]\d+)?)\s*"
52:     r"(billion|million|thousand|B|M|K|bn|mn)?\b",
53:     re.IGNORECASE,
54: )
55: 
56: _DOLLAR_UNIT_SCALE = {
57:     "billion": 1_000_000_000, "bn": 1_000_000_000, "b": 1_000_000_000,
58:     "million": 1_000_000, "mn": 1_000_000, "m": 1_000_000,
59:     "thousand": 1_000, "k": 1_000,
60:     None: 1, "": 1,
61: }
62: 
63: # Years: 4-digit 19xx or 20xx
64: _YEAR_RE = re.compile(r"\b(19\d{2}|20\d{2})\b")
65: 
66: 
67: def _round_dollar_to_bucket(amount: float, tolerance: float = 0.05) -> int:
68:     """Round a dollar amount to a ±5% bucket for signature comparison.
69: 
70:     Example: $11.2B and $11.4B both round to the same bucket (~$11B).
71:               $11.2B and $13.4B fall in different buckets (gap > 5%).
72:     """
73:     if amount <= 0:
74:         return 0
75:     # log-space bucketing: round to nearest 5% step
76:     import math
77:     log_amount = math.log10(amount)
78:     step = math.log10(1 + tolerance)
79:     bucket_idx = round(log_amount / step)
80:     # Return the bucket as an int (representative midpoint)
81:     return int(round(10 ** (bucket_idx * step)))
82: 
83: 
84: @dataclass(frozen=True)
85: class FactSignature:
86:     """Canonical signature for a sentence's quantitative content.
87: 
88:     Two sentences with the SAME signature are candidates for being
89:     duplicate-fact instances. Empty signature (no decimals/dollars/years)
90:     means the sentence has no quantitative content and is NOT a dedup
91:     candidate.
92:     """
93:     decimals: frozenset[float] = field(default_factory=frozenset)
94:     dollar_buckets: frozenset[int] = field(default_factory=frozenset)
95:     years: frozenset[int] = field(default_factory=frozenset)
96: 
97:     def is_empty(self) -> bool:
98:         return not (self.decimals or self.dollar_buckets or self.years)
99: 
100: 
101: def extract_signature(sentence: str) -> FactSignature:
102:     """Extract a FactSignature from a sentence.
103: 
104:     Decimals: floats from percentages.
105:     Dollar buckets: dollar amounts bucketed by ±5% (after unit normalization).
106:     Years: 4-digit 19xx/20xx integers.
107:     """
108:     decimals: set[float] = set()
109:     for match in _PERCENT_RE.finditer(sentence):
110:         try:
111:             decimals.add(round(float(match.group(1)), 2))
112:         except (ValueError, TypeError):
113:             continue
114: 
115:     dollar_buckets: set[int] = set()
116:     for match in _DOLLAR_RE.finditer(sentence):
117:         try:
118:             amount = float(match.group(1).replace(",", ""))
119:         except (ValueError, TypeError):
120:             continue
121:         unit = (match.group(2) or "").lower()
122:         scale = _DOLLAR_UNIT_SCALE.get(unit, 1)
123:         normalized = amount * scale
124:         dollar_buckets.add(_round_dollar_to_bucket(normalized))
125: 
126:     years: set[int] = set()
127:     for match in _YEAR_RE.finditer(sentence):
128:         try:
129:             years.add(int(match.group(1)))
130:         except (ValueError, TypeError):
131:             continue
132: 
133:     return FactSignature(
134:         decimals=frozenset(decimals),
135:         dollar_buckets=frozenset(dollar_buckets),
136:         years=frozenset(years),
137:     )
138: 
139: 
140: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
141: # Grouping + redundancy identification
142: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
143: 
144: 
145: @dataclass
146: class SentenceLocation:
147:     """Pointer to a sentence within section drafts."""
148:     section: str
149:     index: int  # position within the section's sentences list
150:     sentence: str
151:     signature: FactSignature
152: 
153: 
154: @dataclass
155: class RedundancyGroup:
156:     """A group of sentences that share a fact signature."""
157:     signature: FactSignature
158:     primary: SentenceLocation
159:     redundants: list[SentenceLocation]
160: 
161: 
162: def _signatures_overlap(
163:     a: FactSignature, b: FactSignature, min_decimal_overlap: int = 2,
164: ) -> bool:
165:     """Overlap-based signature matcher — per Codex Phase 3 diagnosis.
166: 
167:     Two signatures are considered the same fact unit if they share
168:     EITHER:
169:       - At least `min_decimal_overlap` decimal values (e.g., 9.2% and
170:         13.9% appearing in both → semantic match even if years differ),
171:       - OR they share the COMPLETE decimal set AND have supporting
172:         year/dollar overlap (so a "3.7% in 2016" sentence does NOT match
173:         a "3.7% in 2014" sentence — different timepoints, different
174:         facts),
175:       - OR they share ≥2 dollar buckets.
176: 
177:     Strict pure-decimal match is allowed ONLY when both signatures have
178:     no years and no dollars (so the equality is truly about decimals
179:     alone, not coincidentally-same decimals in different contexts).
180: 
181:     Empty signatures never match.
182: 
183:     Codex iter-1 P1 fix: previously, pure-decimal equality matched even
184:     when years differed → false-positive deduplication risk on facts
185:     that share the same decimal across different timepoints/contexts.
186:     """
187:     if a.is_empty() or b.is_empty():
188:         return False
189:     # Path 0: exact-signature equality (legacy behavior preserved).
190:     # Codex iter-2 P1 regression fix: when two sentences carry the
191:     # IDENTICAL full FactSignature (e.g., both extract as
192:     # FactSignature(dollar_buckets={204}, decimals={}, years={}) for
193:     # "$200 more per person"), they ARE the same fact. The stricter
194:     # iter-1 fix accidentally regressed this case.
195:     if a == b:
196:         return True
197:     # Codex iter-4 P1 fix: populated-axis conflicts must block ALL
198:     # heuristic paths (Path 1/Path 2/Path 3), not just Path 2. Previously
199:     # the guard lived inside Path 2 only, so e.g. "3.0%/1.6% of $40K/$80K
200:     # in 2014" vs "3.0%/1.6% of $200K/$300K in 2014" could still match via
201:     # Path 1's ≥2-decimal shortcut (decimals shared, dollar buckets
202:     # disjoint while years overlap). Lift the guard to a top-level
203:     # precondition so any disjoint populated-axis disqualifies a match.
204:     years_conflict = (a.years and b.years) and not (a.years & b.years)
205:     dollars_conflict = (
206:         (a.dollar_buckets and b.dollar_buckets)
207:         and not (a.dollar_buckets & b.dollar_buckets)
208:     )
209:     if years_conflict or dollars_conflict:
210:         return False
211:     # Path 1: shared salient percentages (≥2 decimals in common)
212:     shared_decimals = a.decimals & b.decimals
213:     if len(shared_decimals) >= min_decimal_overlap:
214:         return True
215:     # Path 2: full decimal-set equality
216:     if a.decimals == b.decimals and a.decimals:
217:         # At least one supporting overlap → match
218:         if a.dollar_buckets & b.dollar_buckets or a.years & b.years:
219:             return True
220:         # Pure decimal-only match: allowed ONLY when both sides have NO
221:         # contextual years AND NO contextual dollars.
222:         if (not a.years and not b.years
223:                 and not a.dollar_buckets and not b.dollar_buckets):
224:             return True
225:         return False
226:     # Path 3: shared dollar buckets (≥2 distinct amounts in common)
227:     shared_dollars = a.dollar_buckets & b.dollar_buckets
228:     if len(shared_dollars) >= 2:
229:         return True
230:     return False
231: 
232: 
233: def _signatures_conflict(a: FactSignature, b: FactSignature) -> bool:
234:     """True iff a populated context axis (years OR dollar_buckets) is
235:     populated on BOTH sides AND has zero intersection.
236: 
237:     Codex brief-iter-1 P1 fix: this is the same populated-axis-conflict
238:     check used by `_signatures_overlap` top-level guard, lifted into a
239:     helper so cluster-membership logic can reject contextless-bridge
240:     merges (e.g. A={2014} and C={2016} merged via B={} bridge).
241:     """
242:     if a.is_empty() or b.is_empty():
243:         return False
244:     years_conflict = (a.years and b.years) and not (a.years & b.years)
245:     dollars_conflict = (
246:         (a.dollar_buckets and b.dollar_buckets)
247:         and not (a.dollar_buckets & b.dollar_buckets)
248:     )
249:     return years_conflict or dollars_conflict
250: 
251: 
252: def _cluster_is_compatible(
253:     candidate: SentenceLocation, cluster: list[SentenceLocation],
254: ) -> bool:
255:     """True iff candidate overlaps with AT LEAST ONE cluster member AND
256:     does NOT conflict with ANY cluster member.
257: 
258:     Phase 3 P1-2 fix (Codex review): previous greedy implementation
259:     compared candidate only against cluster[0]. Comparing against ALL
260:     members captures transitive chains (A↔B↔C where A↛C directly).
261: 
262:     Codex brief-iter-1 P1 fix: requiring "no conflict with any member"
263:     blocks the contextless-bridge merge — e.g. A={9.2%,13.9%,2014} and
264:     C={9.2%,13.9%,2016} would otherwise be merged via B={9.2%,13.9%}
265:     (which overlaps with both and conflicts with neither).
266:     """
267:     has_overlap = False
268:     for member in cluster:
269:         if _signatures_conflict(candidate.signature, member.signature):
270:             return False
271:         if _signatures_overlap(candidate.signature, member.signature):
272:             has_overlap = True
273:     return has_overlap
274: 
275: 
276: def _clusters_pairwise_compatible(
277:     cluster_a: list[SentenceLocation], cluster_b: list[SentenceLocation],
278: ) -> bool:
279:     """True iff no member of cluster_a conflicts with any member of
280:     cluster_b.
281: 
282:     Codex brief-iter-1 P1 fix: when a candidate bridges two existing
283:     clusters X and Y, the candidate may be individually compatible with
284:     both (`_cluster_is_compatible` True for each) while X and Y
285:     themselves contain mutually-conflicting members. Without this
286:     pairwise check, the candidate would silently fuse incompatible
287:     clusters through its contextless overlap.
288:     """
289:     for a in cluster_a:
290:         for b in cluster_b:
291:             if _signatures_conflict(a.signature, b.signature):
292:                 return False
293:     return True
294: 
295: 
296: def build_groups(
297:     sections: dict[str, list[str]],
298:     section_order: Optional[list[str]] = None,
299: ) -> list[RedundancyGroup]:
300:     """Group sentences across sections by overlap-matched FactSignature.
301: 
302:     Per Codex Phase 3 diagnosis (`.codex/I-gen-002-phase3/`): the
303:     earlier exact-FactSignature grouping was too strict — incidental
304:     years/dollars added in one section but not another broke the match.
305:     Now uses `_signatures_overlap` core-fact matcher to group
306:     semantically equivalent sentences even when contextual numerics
307:     differ.
308: 
309:     Args:
310:         sections: dict mapping section_title -> list of sentence strings.
311:         section_order: optional explicit ordering for PRIMARY selection.
312:             If None, falls back to insertion order of `sections` keys.
313: 
314:     Returns:
315:         List of RedundancyGroup, one per overlap-cluster appearing in
316:         2+ section-distinct sentences. Empty signatures are excluded.
317:         Sentences within the same section that share a signature are
318:         NOT counted as redundancy.
319:     """
320:     if section_order is None:

420: def _build_rewrite_prompt(
421:     redundancy_groups: list[RedundancyGroup],
422: ) -> tuple[str, list[tuple[RedundancyGroup, SentenceLocation]]]:
423:     """Build the user prompt + a flat list of (group, redundant_loc) for
424:     aligning the rewrite outputs back to source.
425: 
426:     Returns:
427:         (prompt_text, flat_list_of_input_locations_in_output_order)
428:     """
429:     lines = ["INPUTS (redundant sentence, primary section name):", ""]
430:     flat: list[tuple[RedundancyGroup, SentenceLocation]] = []
431:     counter = 0
432:     for group in redundancy_groups:
433:         for redundant in group.redundants:
434:             counter += 1
435:             lines.append(f"{counter}. REDUNDANT: {redundant.sentence}")
436:             lines.append(f"   PRIMARY_SECTION: {group.primary.section}")
437:             lines.append("")
438:             flat.append((group, redundant))
439:     lines.append(
440:         f"Return JSON {{\"rewrites\": [...]}} with exactly "
441:         f"{counter} entries in the same order as INPUTS."
442:     )
443:     return "\n".join(lines), flat
444: 
445: 
446: async def rewrite_redundant_sentences(
447:     redundancy_groups: list[RedundancyGroup],
448:     llm_callable: Callable[[str, str], Any],
449: ) -> dict[tuple[str, int], Optional[str]]:
450:     """Issue a single LLM call to rewrite all redundant sentences as
451:     cross-references.
452: 
453:     Args:
454:         redundancy_groups: from build_groups().
455:         llm_callable: async callable(system, prompt) -> response object
456:             with .content attribute. Decoupled from openrouter_client
457:             to keep this module test-friendly.
458: 
459:     Returns:
460:         dict mapping (section, index) -> new sentence string OR None if
461:         rewrite failed/null. Caller decides how to handle None
462:         (typically: drop the sentence entirely, keeping only PRIMARY).
463:     """
464:     import json
465: 
466:     if not redundancy_groups:
467:         return {}
468: 
469:     prompt, flat = _build_rewrite_prompt(redundancy_groups)
470:     try:
471:         response = await llm_callable(REWRITE_SYSTEM_PROMPT, prompt)
472:         content = getattr(response, "content", None) or response
473:         # Parse JSON; tolerate code fences
474:         text = str(content).strip()
475:         if text.startswith("```"):
476:             # strip ```json … ``` or ``` … ```
477:             lines = text.splitlines()
478:             text = "\n".join(
479:                 line for line in lines
480:                 if not line.strip().startswith("```")
481:             )
482:         parsed = json.loads(text)
483:         rewrites = parsed.get("rewrites", [])
484:     except (json.JSONDecodeError, AttributeError, KeyError, TypeError) as e:
485:         logger.warning(
486:             "[fact_dedup] rewrite call failed (%s); falling back to "
487:             "DROP-redundants behavior", e,
488:         )
489:         # Safe fallback: drop all redundants (return None for each)
490:         return {(loc.section, loc.index): None for _g, loc in flat}
491: 
492:     if not isinstance(rewrites, list) or len(rewrites) != len(flat):
493:         logger.warning(
494:             "[fact_dedup] rewrite response shape mismatch "
495:             "(expected %d items, got %r); falling back to DROP",
496:             len(flat), type(rewrites).__name__,
497:         )
498:         return {(loc.section, loc.index): None for _g, loc in flat}
499: 
500:     out: dict[tuple[str, int], Optional[str]] = {}
501:     for (_group, loc), rewrite in zip(flat, rewrites):
502:         if isinstance(rewrite, str) and rewrite.strip():
503:             out[(loc.section, loc.index)] = rewrite.strip()
504:         else:
505:             # null/empty rewrite → drop
506:             out[(loc.section, loc.index)] = None
507:     return out
508: 
509: 
510: def apply_rewrites(
511:     sections: dict[str, list[str]],
512:     rewrites: dict[tuple[str, int], Optional[str]],
513: ) -> dict[str, list[str]]:
514:     """Apply rewrites in-place-equivalent (returns new dict).
515: 
516:     None rewrites = drop the sentence from its section.
517:     String rewrites = replace the sentence at that (section, index).
518:     """
519:     new_sections: dict[str, list[str]] = {}
520:     for section_title, sentences in sections.items():
521:         new_sentences: list[str] = []
522:         for idx, sentence in enumerate(sentences):
523:             key = (section_title, idx)
524:             if key in rewrites:
525:                 replacement = rewrites[key]
526:                 if replacement is None:
527:                     # Drop redundant entirely
528:                     continue
529:                 new_sentences.append(replacement)
530:             else:
531:                 new_sentences.append(sentence)
532:         new_sections[section_title] = new_sentences
533:     return new_sections
534:

536: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
537: # Top-level entry point
538: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

541: async def dedup_pass(
542:     sections: dict[str, list[str]],
543:     llm_callable: Callable[[str, str], Any],
544:     section_order: Optional[list[str]] = None,
545: ) -> tuple[dict[str, list[str]], dict[str, Any]]:
546:     """End-to-end dedup pass.
547: 
548:     Args:
549:         sections: dict mapping section_title -> list of sentence strings.
550:             Typically the verified sentences from each section after
551:             multi_section generation.
552:         llm_callable: async callable(system, prompt) -> response.
553:         section_order: explicit PRIMARY ordering; defaults to insertion.
554: 
555:     Returns:
556:         (new_sections, telemetry) where telemetry includes:
557:             - n_groups: number of duplicate-fact groups detected
558:             - n_redundants: total redundant sentences flagged
559:             - n_rewrites_applied: successful rewrites
560:             - n_drops: sentences dropped because rewrite returned None
561:     """
562:     groups = build_groups(sections, section_order=section_order)
563:     n_redundants = count_redundancy(groups)
564:     telemetry: dict[str, Any] = {
565:         "n_groups": len(groups),
566:         "n_redundants": n_redundants,
567:         "n_rewrites_applied": 0,
568:         "n_drops": 0,
569:     }
570:     if not groups:
571:         return sections, telemetry
572: 
573:     logger.info(
574:         "[fact_dedup] %d duplicate-fact groups detected, "
575:         "%d redundant sentences to rewrite",
576:         len(groups), n_redundants,
577:     )
578:     rewrites = await rewrite_redundant_sentences(groups, llm_callable)
579:     for _k, v in rewrites.items():
580:         if v is None:
581:             telemetry["n_drops"] += 1
582:         else:
583:             telemetry["n_rewrites_applied"] += 1
584: 
585:     new_sections = apply_rewrites(sections, rewrites)
586:     logger.info(
587:         "[fact_dedup] applied=%d, dropped=%d",
588:         telemetry["n_rewrites_applied"], telemetry["n_drops"],
589:     )
590:     return new_sections, telemetry

57: def numbers_present(sentence: str, span: str) -> tuple[bool, list[str]]:
58:     """Every numeric token in the sentence must appear in the span (§-1.1)."""
59:     nums = _NUM.findall(_norm(sentence))
60:     span_n = _norm(span)
61:     missing = [n for n in nums if n not in span_n]
62:     return (len(missing) == 0, missing)

843:     _require_keys(raw, ("sections", "totals"), "verification_details.json")
844:     if not isinstance(raw["sections"], list):
845:         raise AuditIRSchemaError("verification_details.json: 'sections' must be a list")

867:             )

      The new serializer trusts SectionResult.kept_sentences_pre_resolve and dropped_sentences_final, but contract sections still instantiate SectionResult without populating either field. In PG_V30_PHASE2_ENABLED runs, contract sections can emit verified_text and nonzero sentences_verified, while verification_details.json will serialize total_in=0, kept=[], dropped=[] for those sections. That preserves the artifact/totals mismatch class from the smoke P1.
    proposed_fix: |
      In run_contract_section, pass kept_sentences_pre_resolve=final kept_sentences and dropped_sentences_final=final non-rescued dropped sentences into section_result_cls. Remove rescued SVs from dropped_sentences_final because they are final kept sentences.
  - severity: P1
    location: src/polaris_graph/generator/multi_section_generator.py:1426
    issue: |
      M-41c drops strict-verified under-framed trial sentences after verification, but Step 1.5 does not persist report_dropped_m41c into any final drop category. Those sentences disappear from kept[] and dropped[]/dedup[], so verification_details.json is still not a complete final per-sentence accounting when M-41c fires.
    proposed_fix: |
      Add a final policy-drop category such as dropped_sentences_m41c_underframed, populate it from report_dropped_m41c, serialize it separately, and include it in section total_dropped/total_in rollups.
  - severity: P1
    location: src/polaris_graph/generator/multi_section_generator.py:3887
    issue: |
      Dedup accounting updates sr.sentences_dropped by net length delta, but serialization counts every original sentence placed in dropped_sentences_dedup_redundant. For accepted 1:1 dedup rewrites, sr.sentences_dropped increases by 0 while verification_details section total_dropped increases by 1, recreating section-vs-artifact total mismatch.
    proposed_fix: |
      Define dedup replacement semantics consistently. If dropped_by_dedup_redundant counts replaced originals as drops, increment sr.sentences_dropped by that same count and align multi.total_sentences_dropped with serialized section totals. Also cover failed rewrite candidates consistently.
novel_p0: []
